<A NAME="toc15649_14"></A>Item&nbsp;9. Changes in and Disagreements with Accountants on Accounting and Financial Disclosure </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">On October&nbsp;18, 2005,
the Board of Directors of Preferred dismissed Arthur F. Bell, Jr.&nbsp;&amp; Associates, L.L.C. (&#147;AFB&#148;) as the independent registered public accounting firm for the Registrant. The report of AFB on the Registrant&#146;s financial
statements as of and for the fiscal year ended December&nbsp;31, 2004 did not contain an adverse opinion or a disclaimer of opinion, and was not qualified or modified as to uncertainties, audit scope, or accounting principles. AFB was engaged by
World Monitor Trust &#150; Series A on October&nbsp;1, 2004. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">During the Registrant&#146;s most recent fiscal year ended December&nbsp;31, 2004 and during
the period from the end of the most recently completed fiscal year through the date of this Form 8-K, the Registrant and the Managing Owner have had no disagreements with AFB on any matter of accounting principles or practices, financial statement
disclosure, or auditing scope or procedure, which disagreement(s), if not resolved to the satisfaction of AFB, would have caused it to make a reference to the subject matter thereof in its report on the financial statements of the Registrant for
such period. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">On October&nbsp;18, 2005, the Board of Directors of the Managing Owner, on behalf of the Registrant, approved the engagement of
Deloitte&nbsp;&amp; Touche LLP (&#147;D&amp;T&#148;) as the independent registered public accounting firm for the Registrant. During the Registrant&#146;s two most recent fiscal years and the interim period prior to engaging D&amp;T, neither the
Registrant, the Managing Owner, nor anyone on their behalf consulted D&amp;T, on behalf of the Registrant, regarding the application of accounting principles to a specified transaction (either completed or proposed), the type of audit opinion that
might be rendered on the Registrant&#146;s financial statements, or any matter that was either the subject of a &#147;disagreement,&#148; as defined in Item&nbsp;304(a)(1)(iv) of Regulation S-K and the instructions thereto, or a &#147;reportable
event,&#148; as defined in Item&nbsp;304(a)(1)(v) of Regulation S-K. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>
<A NAME="toc15649_15"></A>Item&nbsp;9A. Controls and Procedures </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">As of the end of the period covered by this report, the Managing Owner carried out an
evaluation, under the supervision and with the participation of the officers of the Managing Owner, including the Managing Owner&#146;s chief executive officer, chief financial officer and director of fund administration, of the effectiveness of the
design and operation of the Registrant&#146;s disclosure controls and procedures. Based upon that evaluation, the Managing Owner&#146;s chief executive officer, chief financial officer and director of fund administration concluded that the
Registrants disclosure controls and procedures are effective. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>

<A NAME="toc15649_18"></A>Item&nbsp;10. Directors and Executive Officer of the Registrant </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:2%; text-indent:-2%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">There are no officers of the
Registrant. The Registrant is managed by the Managing Owner. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:2%; text-indent:-2%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The key officers of the Managing Owner and their positions
with respect to the Registrant are as follows: </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Mr.&nbsp;Kenneth&nbsp;A. Shewer</B> (born 1953), has been a principal, associated person and NFA
associate member of the Managing Owner since February&nbsp;8, 1984,&nbsp;May&nbsp;1,1985 since August&nbsp;1, 1985, respectively. He has been Chairman and Co-Chief Executive Officer of the Managing Owner since February 1984. Mr.&nbsp;Shewer was
employed by Pasternak, Baum and Co., Inc. (&#147;Pasternak, Baum&#148;), an international cash commodity firm, from June 1976 until September 1983. Mr.&nbsp;Shewer created and managed Pasternak, Baum&#146;s Grain Logistics and Administration
Department and created its Domestic Corn and Soybean Trading Department. Mr.&nbsp;Shewer&#146;s responsibilities at Pasternak, Baum included merchandising South American grain and exporting United States corn and soybeans. In 1982, Mr.&nbsp;Shewer
became co-manager of Pasternak, Baum&#146;s F.O.B. Corn Department. In 1983, Mr.&nbsp;Shewer was made Vice President and Director of Pasternak, Baum. Mr.&nbsp;Shewer has traveled extensively in South America and Europe in connection with the
commodity business and has organized and effected grain and oilseed sales in those regions, the former Soviet Union, and the Far East. While at Pasternak, Baum, Mr.&nbsp;Shewer was a member of the St. Louis Merchants Exchange and was associated with
the National Grain and Feed Association and the North American Export Grain Association. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Mr.&nbsp;Shewer graduated from Syracuse University with a B.S.
degree in 1975. Mr.&nbsp;Shewer sits on the Board of the Stacy Joy Goodman Memorial Foundation, a non-profit charity committed to finding a cure for Juvenile Diabetes. He is also a member of the Board of the Diabetes Research Institute Foundation, a
not-for-profit organization affiliated with the University of Miami School of Medicine. Mr.&nbsp;Shewer is a founding member and member of the Board of the Greenwich Roundtable. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Mr.&nbsp;Marc&nbsp;S. Goodman</B> (born 1948) has been a principal, associated person and NFA associate member of the Managing Owner since February&nbsp;7, 1984,&nbsp;May&nbsp;1, 1985 since August&nbsp;1, 1985,
respectively. He has been President and Co-Chief Executive Officer of the Managing Owner since February 1984. Mr.&nbsp;Goodman joined Pasternak, Baum in September 1974 and was a Vice President and Director from July 1981 until September 1983. While
at Pasternak, Baum, Mr.&nbsp;Goodman was largely responsible for business development outside of the United States, for investment of its corporate retirement funds, and for selecting trading personnel in the Vegetable Oil Division Mr.&nbsp;Goodman
also created and developed Pasternak, Baum&#146;s Laric Oils Department. Mr.&nbsp;Goodman has conducted extensive business in South America, Europe and the Far East; he has been a merchandiser of all major vegetable oils and their by-products, and
of various other commodities such as sunflower seeds, frozen poultry, pulses and potatoes. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Mr.&nbsp;Goodman graduated from the Bernard M. Baruch School of
Business of the City University of New York with a B.B.A. in 1969 and an M.B.A. in 1971 in Finance and Investments, where he was awarded an Economics and Finance Department Fellowship from September 1969 through June 1971. Mr.&nbsp;Goodman is a
member of the American Arbitration Association; while at Pasternak, Baum, he was a member of the National Institute of Oilseeds Products and the American Fats and Oils Association (including its Export Rules Committee). </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Mr.&nbsp;Goodman is the Chairman of the Board of the Stacy Joy Goodman Memorial Foundation, a non-profit charity committed to finding a cure for Juvenile Diabetes. He is
also Chairman of the Board of the Diabetes Research Institute Foundation, a not-for-profit organization which is the principle source of funding for the Diabetes Research Institute, a world renowned cure based research center affiliated with the
University of Miami School of Medicine. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Mr.&nbsp;Goodman is a founding member and member of the Board of the Greenwich Roundtable and is a member of the
Board of Xethanol Corp. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Messrs. Shewer and Goodman left Pasternak, Baum in September 1983 to form Kenmar Advisory Corp. (now known as Preferred Investment
Solutions Corp., the Managing Owner) and they have occupied their present positions with the Managing Owner since that time. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Ms.&nbsp;Esther Eckerling Goodman</B> (born 1952) has been a principal, associated person and NFA associate member of
the Managing Owner since May&nbsp;12, 1988,&nbsp;July&nbsp;17, 1986 and July&nbsp;17, 1986, respectively. She joined the Managing Owner in July 1986 and is its Chief Operating Officer and Senior Executive Vice President. Ms.&nbsp;Goodman has been
involved in the futures industry since 1974. From 1974 through 1976, she was employed by Conti-Commodity Services, Inc. and ACLI Commodity Services, Inc., in the areas of hedging, speculative trading and tax arbitrage. In 1976, Ms.&nbsp;Goodman
joined Loeb Rhoades&nbsp;&amp; Company, Inc. where she was responsible for developing and managing a managed futures program which, in 1979, became the trading system for Westchester Commodity Management, an independent commodity-trading advisor of
which Ms.&nbsp;Goodman was a founder and principal. From 1983 through mid-1986, Ms.&nbsp;Goodman was employed as a marketing executive at Commodities Corp. (USA) of Princeton, New Jersey. Ms.&nbsp;Goodman was a Director of the Managed Futures Trade
Association from 1987 to 1991 and a Director of its successor organization, the Managed Futures Association, from 1991 to 1995 (now the Managed Funds Association). Ms.&nbsp;Goodman graduated from Stanford University with a B.A. degree in psychology
in 1974. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Mr.&nbsp;Braxton Glasgow III</B> (born 1953), has been a principal, associated person, branch manager and NFA associate member of the Managing
Owner since June&nbsp;21, 2001,&nbsp;June&nbsp;21, 2001,&nbsp;July&nbsp;13, 2004 and June&nbsp;8, 2001, respectively. Mr.&nbsp;Glasgow has been an Executive Vice President of the Managing Owner since joining the Managing Owner in May 2001.
Mr.&nbsp;Glasgow is responsible for business development. Previously, he served as Executive Vice President, Director of Client Services and a Principal at Chesapeake Capital Corp., a commodities trading firm, and as Senior Managing Director at
Signet Investment Banking Co. Mr.&nbsp;Glasgow began his career at PricewaterhouseCoopers, where he specialized in mergers and acquisitions and private equity, including extensive work in Europe and the Far East. Mr.&nbsp;Glasgow received a B.S. in
Accounting from the University of North Carolina at Chapel Hill and is a Certified Public Accountant. From 1994 to 1995, he was President of the Jay Group Ltd. Mr.&nbsp;Glasgow received a B.S. degree in accounting from the University of North
Carolina in 1975. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Ms.&nbsp;Maureen&nbsp;D. Howley</B> (born 1967), has been a principal of the Managing Owner since August&nbsp;11, 2003. She has been
a Senior Vice President and Chief Financial Officer of the Managing Owner since joining the Managing Owner in July 2003. She is responsible for corporate finance. From July 2001 until July 2003, Ms.&nbsp;Howley was an Associate at Andor Capital
Management, LLC, an equity hedge fund company. At Andor, she was responsible for managing the corporate accounting functions. Previously, she was the Controller at John W. Henry&nbsp;&amp; Company, Inc., a commodity-trading advisor
(&#147;JWH&#148;), where she held positions of increasing responsibility from September 1996 to July 2001. She began her career at Deloitte&nbsp;&amp; Touche where she specialized in the financial services industry. She held many positions of
increasing responsibility for seven years, and left as an Audit Senior Manager in September 1996 to join JWH. Ms.&nbsp;Howley received a B.A. in Accounting from Muhlenberg College in 1989 and designation as a Certified Public Accountant in 1990.
</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Mr.&nbsp;Lawrence&nbsp;S. Block</B> (born 1967) has been a Senior Vice President and General Counsel of the Managing Owner since joining the Managing

University of Pennsylvania School of Law in 1992. Mr.&nbsp;Block&#146;s registration as a principal of the Managing Owner has been effective since March&nbsp;17, 2005. His registration as an Associated Person of the Managing Owner is pending with
the National Futures Association. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Ms.&nbsp;Joanne&nbsp;D. Rosenthal</B> (born 1965), has been a principal, associated person and NFA associate member
of the Managing Owner since February&nbsp;29, 2000,&nbsp;February&nbsp;29, 2000 and November&nbsp;30, 1999, respectively. Ms.&nbsp;Rosenthal is Senior Vice President and Director of Portfolio Management and Implementation for the Managing Owner.
Prior to joining the Managing Owner in October 1999, Ms.&nbsp;Rosenthal spent nine years at The Chase Manhattan Bank, in various positions of increasing responsibility. From July 1991 through April 1994, she managed the Trade Execution Desk and from
May 1994 through September 1999, she was a Vice President and Senior Portfolio Manager of Chase Alternative Asset Management, Inc. Ms.&nbsp;Rosenthal received a Masters of Business Administration with a concentration in Finance from Cornell
University and a Bachelor of Arts in Economics from Concordia University in Montreal, Canada. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Mr.&nbsp;Peter&nbsp;J. Fell</B> (born 1960), Senior Vice
President, Director of Due Diligence since joining the Managing Owner in September 2004. He is responsible for manager selection and due diligence. Mr.&nbsp;Fell is a member of the Investment Committee. From 2000 through August 2004, Mr.&nbsp;Fell
was a founding partner and Investment Director of Starview Capital Management. Prior to co-founding Starview Capital Management, Mr.&nbsp;Fell was Vice President of Research and Product Development at Merrill Lynch Investment Partners Inc (MLIP). He
was responsible for the investment evaluation and recommendation process pertaining to MLIP funds and sat on MLIP&#146;s Investment Committee. Prior to joining MLIP, Mr.&nbsp;Fell had been with Deutsche Bank Financial Products Corporation for six
years starting in 1989, where he was Vice President in the over-the-counter fixed income derivatives area. From 1985 to 1989, he was employed by Manufacturers Hanover Trust Company, ultimately holding the position of Assistant Vice President in the
Swaps and Futures Group. Mr.&nbsp;Fell holds an A.B. cum laude in Music Theory and History and an M.B.A. in Finance from Columbia University. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>

FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Certain of the Managing Owner&#146;s directors and officers and any persons holding more than ten percent of the Registrant&#146;s Limited Interests (&#147;Ten Percent Owners&#148;) are required to report their
initial ownership of such Limited Interests and any subsequent changes in that ownership to the Securities and Exchange Commission (the &#147;SEC&#148;) on Forms 3, 4 or 5. Such directors and officers and Ten Percent Owners are required by SEC
regulations to furnish the Registrant with copies of all Forms 3, 4 and 5 they file. There are no Ten Percent Owners of the Registrant&#146;s Limited Interests. Each of Lawrence S. Block and David K. Spohr failed to timely file an Initial Statement
of Beneficial Ownership of Securities on Form 3 during the Registrant&#146;s most recent fiscal year. Other than as set forth above, all filing requirements of Section&nbsp;16(a) of the Exchange Act were timely complied with during the fiscal year.
In making these disclosures, the Registrant has relied solely on written representations of the Managing Owner&#146;s directors and officers and the Registrant&#146;s Ten Percent Owners or copies of the reports that they have filed with the SEC
during and with respect to its most recent fiscal year. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:2%; text-indent:-2%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B><U>Audit Committee Financial Expert</U></B> </FONT></P> <P

Controls and Disclosure Committee, serves as the &#147;audit committee financial expert&#148; for Preferred Investment Solutions Corp. Ms.&nbsp;Howley is not a member of the Board of Directors and she is not independent of management. </FONT></P> <P

<A NAME="toc15649_21"></A>Item&nbsp;13. Certain Relationships and Related Transactions </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Registrant has and will continue to have certain
relationships with the Managing Owner and its affiliates. However, there have been no direct financial transactions between the Registrant and the officers of the Managing Owner. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Reference is made to Notes 1, 3 and 4 to the financial statements in the Registrant&#146;s 2005 Annual Report which is filed as an exhibit hereto, which identify the related parties and discuss the services provided
by these parties and the amounts paid or payable for their services. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>
<A NAME="toc15649_22"></A>Item&nbsp;14. Principal Accounting Fees and Services </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Audit Fees and All Other Fees </B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The principle accountant for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2005 was Deloitte&nbsp;&amp; Touche LLP. The principle accountant for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2004
was Arthur F. Bell, Jr.&nbsp;&amp; Associates, L.L.C. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>Audit Fees </I></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Fees for audit services totaled approximately $31,000 for 2005 ($20,000 to Deloitte&nbsp;&amp; Touche LLP and $11,000 to Arthur F. Bell, Jr.&nbsp;&amp; Associates, L.L.C.) and $28,000 during 2004, respectively,
including fees associated with the annual audit and the reviews of the Registrant&#146;s quarterly reports on Form 10-Q. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>

services by Arthur F. Bell, Jr.&nbsp;&amp; Associates, L.L.C, including tax compliance and tax advice totaled approximately $7,000 and $6,500 in 2005 and 2004, respectively. The Managing Owner will pay the audit and tax fees as well as all the
administrative costs incurred by the Registrant, as further discussed in Note 3 of the Registrant&#146;s 2005 Annual Report. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">We have been advised by

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>REPORT OF INDEPENDENT REGISTERED PUBLIC ACCOUNTING FIRM </B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:2%; text-indent:-2%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">To the Managing Owner and Limited Interest Owners of </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:2%; text-indent:-2%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">World Monitor Trust &#150; Series A </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">We have
audited the accompanying statement of financial condition, including the condensed schedule of investments, of World Monitor Trust &#150; Series A (the &#147;Trust&#148;) as of December&nbsp;31, 2005, and the related statements of operations and
changes in Unitholders&#146; capital for the year then ended. These financial statements are the responsibility of the Trust&#146;s management. Our responsibility is to express an opinion on these financial statements based on our audit. The
financial statements for the years ended December&nbsp;31, 2004 and 2003, including the condensed schedule of investments for 2004, were audited by other auditors whose reports dated March&nbsp;25, 2005 and January&nbsp;23, 2004, respectively,
expressed unqualified opinions on those statements. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">We conducted our audit in accordance with the standards of the Public Company Accounting Oversight
Board (United States). Those standards require that we plan and perform the audit to obtain reasonable assurance about whether the financial statements are free of material misstatement. The Trust is not required to have, nor were we engaged to
perform, an audit of its internal control over financial reporting. Our audit included consideration of internal control over financial reporting as a basis for designing audit procedures that are appropriate in the circumstances, but not for the
purpose of expressing an opinion on the effectiveness of the Trust&#146;s internal control over financial reporting. Accordingly, we express no such opinion. An audit also includes examining, on a test basis, evidence supporting the amounts and
disclosures in the financial statements, assessing the accounting principles used and significant estimates made by management, as well as evaluating the overall financial statement presentation. We believe that our audit provides a reasonable basis
for our opinion. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">In our opinion, the 2005 financial statements referred to above present fairly, in all material respects, the financial position of the
Trust at December&nbsp;31, 2005, and the results of its operations and changes in Unitholders&#146; capital for the year then ended in conformity with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States of America. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:2%; text-indent:-2%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">/s/ Deloitte&nbsp;&amp; Touche LLP </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:2%; text-indent:-2%"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">March&nbsp;29, 2006 </FONT></P>

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>WORLD MONITOR TRUST &#150; SERIES A </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"
ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>NOTES TO FINANCIAL STATEMENTS </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P><HR WIDTH="17%" SIZE="1" NOSHADE COLOR="#000000"> <P

<TR>
<TD WIDTH="8%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Note&nbsp;1.</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><U>ORGANIZATION</U> </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="8%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="5%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">A.</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">General Description of the Trust </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">World Monitor Trust
&#150; Series A (the &#147;Trust&#148;) is a business trust organized under the laws of Delaware on December&nbsp;17, 1997. The Trust commenced trading operations on June&nbsp;10, 1998 and will terminate on December&nbsp;31, 2047 unless terminated
sooner as provided in the Third Amended and Restated Declaration of Trust and Trust Agreement. The Trust consists of three separate and distinct series (&#147;Series&#148;): Series A, B and C. The assets of each Series are segregated from those of
the other Series, separately valued and independently managed. Each Series was formed to engage in the speculative trading of a diversified portfolio of futures, forward and options contracts and may, from time to time, engage in cash and spot
transactions. The trustee of the Trust is Wilmington Trust Company. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">On July&nbsp;1, 2003, Prudential Financial, Inc.
(&#147;Prudential&#148;) and Wachovia Corp. (&#147;Wachovia&#148;) combined their separate retail securities brokerage and clearing businesses under a new holding company named Wachovia/Prudential Financial Advisors, LLC (&#147;WPFA&#148;), owned
62% by Wachovia and 38% by Prudential. As a result, the retail brokerage operations of Prudential Securities Incorporated (&#147;PSI&#148;) were contributed to Wachovia Securities, LLC (&#147;Wachovia Securities&#148;). Wachovia Securities is
wholly-owned by WPFA and is a registered broker-dealer and a member of the National Association of Securities Dealers, Inc. (&#147;NASD&#148;) and all major securities exchanges. Series A and its Managing Owner, Prudential Securities Futures
Management, Inc., which was an indirect wholly-owned subsidiary of PSI, entered into a service agreement with Wachovia Securities, effective July&nbsp;1, 2003. Pursuant to this agreement, Wachovia Securities agreed to provide certain enumerated
services to accounts of the limited interest owners carried at Wachovia. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Effective July&nbsp;1, 2003, PSI changed its name to Prudential
Equity Group, Inc. (&#147;PEG&#148;). PEG remained an indirectly wholly-owned subsidiary of Prudential. PEG was a registered broker-dealer and a member of the NASD and all major securities exchanges and conducted the equity research, domestic and
international equity sales and trading operations, and commodity brokerage and derivative operations it had previously conducted as PSI until December&nbsp;31, 2003. As part of the process of reorganizing its business structure, Prudential
Securities Group Inc. (&#147;PSG&#148;), the direct parent of PEG and a wholly-owned subsidiary of Prudential, transferred the commodity brokerage, commodity clearing and derivative operations previously performed by PEG to another PSG indirect
wholly-owned subsidiary, Prudential Financial Derivatives, LLC (&#147;PFD&#148;) effective January&nbsp;1, 2004. Like PEG, PFD is registered as a futures commission merchant under the Commodity Exchange Act and is a member of the National Futures
Association. On April&nbsp;1, 2004, PEG transferred the ownership of the Managing Owner and PFD Holdings, LLC, the direct parent of PFD to PSG. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">-8- </FONT></P>

<TD WIDTH="8%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Note&nbsp;1.</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><U>ORGANIZATION (CONTINUED)</U> </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="8%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="5%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">A.</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">General Description of the Trust (continued) </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">On
June&nbsp;30, 2004, PSG and Preferred Investment Solutions Corp., formerly Kenmar Advisory Corp. (&#147;Preferred&#148;), entered into a Stock Purchase Agreement, pursuant to which PSG would sell, and Preferred would buy, all of the capital stock of
Prudential Securities Futures Management Inc. (the then current Managing Owner of Series A) and another commodity pool operator owned by PSG. In connection with the transaction, Prudential Securities Futures Management, Inc. solicited proxies
seeking approval from the Series A interest holders for (i)&nbsp;the sale of the stock of Prudential Securities Futures Management, Inc. to Preferred; (ii)&nbsp;the concomitant approval of Preferred as the new Managing Owner of Series A; and
(iii)&nbsp;the concomitant approval of certain amendments to the Declaration of Trust and Trust Agreement of the Trust. A Report on Form 8-K describing the transaction was filed with the Securities and Exchange Commission on July&nbsp;1, 2004 and
the definitive proxies were filed with the Securities and Exchange Commission on July&nbsp;20, 2004. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">As of October&nbsp;1, 2004, Preferred
acquired from PSG all of the outstanding stock of Prudential Securities Futures Management Inc. Immediately after such acquisition, Prudential Securities Futures Management Inc. was merged with and into Preferred. Accordingly, as of October&nbsp;1,
2004 all of the board of directors and officers of Prudential Securities Futures Management Inc. resigned. Following Preferred&#146;s acquisition of Prudential Securities Futures Management, Inc. and its merger with and into Preferred, Preferred
became the successor Managing Owner of Series A. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The term Managing Owner, as used herein, refers either to Prudential Securities Futures
Management Inc. or Preferred, depending upon the applicable period discussed. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Effective December&nbsp;6, 2004, Series A contributed its
net assets to WMT Campbell Pool L.L.C. (the &#147;Company&#148;) and received a Voting Membership Interest in the Company. The Company was formed to function as an aggregate trading vehicle. The sole members of the Company are Series A and World
Monitor Trust II &#150; Series F (&#147;Series F&#148;). Preferred is the Managing Owner of Series F and has been delegated administrative authority over the operations of the Company. The Company engages in the speculative trading of futures
contracts. The financial statements of the Company, including the condensed schedule of investments, are included in Section II of these financial statements and should be used in conjunction with Series A&#146;s financial statements. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">

<TD WIDTH="8%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="5%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">B.</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Regulation </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">As a registrant with the Securities and
Exchange Commission, the Trust is subject to the regulatory requirements under the Securities Act of 1933 and the Securities Exchange Act of 1934. As a commodity pool, the Trust is subject to the regulations of the Commodity Futures Trading
Commission, an agency of the United States (U.S.) government which regulates most aspects of the commodity futures industry; rules of the National Futures Association, an industry self-regulatory organization; and the requirements of the various
commodity exchanges where the Trust executes transactions. Additionally, the Trust is subject to the requirements of the futures commission merchants (brokers) and interbank market makers through which the Trust trades. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">-9- </FONT></P>

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>WORLD MONITOR TRUST &#150; SERIES A </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"
ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>NOTES TO FINANCIAL STATEMENTS (CONTINUED) </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P><HR WIDTH="17%" SIZE="1" NOSHADE COLOR="#000000"> <P

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><U>ORGANIZATION (CONTINUED)</U> </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>

<TD WIDTH="8%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="5%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">C.</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Offering </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Beneficial interests in each Series
(&#147;Interests&#148;) were offered once each week until each Series&#146; subscription maximum was met either through sale or exchange or until the Managing Owner suspended the offering of Interests. On June&nbsp;10, 1998, a sufficient number of
subscriptions for each Series had been received and accepted by the Managing Owner to permit each Series to commence trading. World Monitor Trust &#150; Series A (&#147;Series A&#148;) completed its initial offering with gross proceeds of $6,039,177
from the sale of 59,631.775 Limited Interests and 760 of General Interests. General Interests were sold exclusively to the Managing Owner. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="2">Series A was offered until it achieved its subscription maximum of $34,000,000 during November 1999. Interests in World Monitor Trust &#150; Series B (&#147;Series B&#148;) and World Monitor Trust &#150; Series C (&#147;Series C&#148;)
continued to be offered on a weekly basis at the then current net asset value per interest until the Managing Owner suspended the offering of Interests for each Series. The Managing Owner suspended the offering of Interests in Series B and Series C
and allowed all selling registrations to expire by April&nbsp;30, 2002. Series C was liquidated effective September&nbsp;20, 2004. As such, Interests owned in one series of the Trust may no longer be exchanged for Interests of one or more other
Series. While the Managing Owner does not anticipate doing so, it may, at its election, reinstate the offering of Interests in Series A in the future. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Managing Owner is required to maintain at least 1% interest in the capital, profits and losses of each Series so long as it is acting as the Managing Owner, and it will make such contribution (and in return
receive general interests) as are necessary to meet this requirement. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="8%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="5%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">D.</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Trading Advisor </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Each Series has its own independent
commodity trading advisor that makes that Series trading decisions. The Managing Owner has allocated 100% of the proceeds from the initial and continuous offering of Series A to its trading advisor. The Managing Owner, on behalf of Series A,
initially entered into an advisory agreement (the &#147;Initial Advisory Agreement&#148;) with Eagle Trading Systems, Inc. (the &#147;Trading Advisor&#148;) to make the trading decisions for Series A utilizing both the Eagle-Global System and the
Eagle-FX System. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Effective December&nbsp;6, 1999, the Eagle-Global System became the exclusive trading program used by the Trading Advisor
to trade Series A&#146;s assets. In conjunction with this change, the Managing Owner and the Trading Advisor voluntarily agreed to terminate the Initial Advisory Agreement and enter into a new advisory agreement (the &#147;New Advisory
Agreement&#148;) effective March&nbsp;21, 2000. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">-10- </FONT></P>

ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>NOTES TO FINANCIAL STATEMENTS (CONTINUED) </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P><HR WIDTH="17%" SIZE="1" NOSHADE COLOR="#000000"> <P

<TD WIDTH="8%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Note&nbsp;1.</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><U>ORGANIZATION (CONTINUED)</U> </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="8%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="5%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">D.</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Trading Advisor (continued) </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Pursuant to the New
Advisory Agreement, the Trading Advisor was paid a weekly management fee at an annual rate of 1% of Series A&#146;s net asset value until the net asset value per Interest was at least $80 for a period of at least 10 consecutive business days, at
which time the weekly management fee was to be increased to an annual rate of 2% (i.e., the rate pursuant to the Initial Advisory Agreement). Effective October&nbsp;31, 2001, Series A sustained a new asset value per Interest greater than $80 for 10
consecutive business days. As a result, the Trading Advisor was paid a weekly management fee at an annual rate of 2% since November&nbsp;1, 2001. Series A also pays its Trading Advisor a quarterly incentive fee equal to 23% of the Registrant&#146;s
&#147;New High Net Trading Profits&#148; (as defined in the New Advisory Agreement). The Incentive fee accrues weekly. Additionally, although the term of the New Advisory Agreement commenced on March&nbsp;21, 2000, the Trading Advisor must recoup
all trading losses incurred under the Initial Advisory Agreement before an incentive fee is paid. Furthermore, the New Advisory Agreement resets the net asset value for purposes of its termination provisions. The New Advisory Agreement may be
terminated for a variety of reasons, including at the discretion of the Managing Owner. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Effective August&nbsp;30, 2004, Eagle Trading
Systems was removed as the trading advisor of Series A because the trading advisor experienced losses in excess of 33<FONT SIZE="1"><SUP>&nbsp;1</SUP></FONT><FONT SIZE="2">/</FONT><FONT SIZE="1">3</FONT><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"
COLOR="#000000">% since January&nbsp;1, 2004. For the period from August&nbsp;30, 2004 through December&nbsp;6, 2004, the assets of Series A remained in cash at its broker. As of December&nbsp;6, 2004, Series A&#146;s assets were invested in the WMT
Campbell Pool L.L.C. </FONT></FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>

<TD WIDTH="5%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">E.</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Exchanges, Redemptions and Termination </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">As a result of
the Managing Owner suspending the offering of Interests in Series B and Series C as discussed in Note C, Interests owned in one series of the Trust (Series A, B or C) may no longer be exchanged for Interests of one or more other Series. </FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Redemptions are permitted on a weekly basis at the then current net asset value per Interest. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">In the event that the estimated net asset value per Interest of a Series at the end of any business day, after adjustments for distributions, declines by
50% or more since the commencement of trading activities or the first day of a fiscal year, Series A will terminate. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:18px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>

<TD WIDTH="5%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">A.</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Basis of Accounting </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The financial statements of Series A
are prepared in accordance with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States of America. Such principles require the Managing Owner to make estimates and assumptions that affect the reported amounts of assets and liabilities and
disclosure of contingent assets and liabilities at the date of the financial statements and the reported amounts of revenues and expenses during the reporting period. Actual results could differ from these estimates. </FONT></P> <P

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>WORLD MONITOR TRUST &#150; SERIES A </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"
ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>NOTES TO FINANCIAL STATEMENTS (CONTINUED) </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P><HR WIDTH="17%" SIZE="1" NOSHADE COLOR="#000000"> <P
STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>

<TR>
<TD WIDTH="8%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Note&nbsp;2.</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><U>SUMMARY OF SIGNIFICANT ACCOUNTING POLICIES (CONTINUED)</U> </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="8%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="5%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">A.</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Basis of Accounting (continued) </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Commodity futures and
forward transactions are reflected in the accompanying statements of financial condition on trade date. Net unrealized gain or loss on open contracts (the difference between contract trade price and market price) is reflected in the statement of
financial condition in accordance with Financial Accounting Standards Board Interpretation No.&nbsp;39 &#150; &#147;Offsetting of Amounts Related to Certain Contracts.&#148; The market value of futures (exchange-traded) contracts is based upon the
closing quotation on the various futures exchanges on which the contract is traded. The values which will be used by Series A for its open forward positions will be provided by its administrator, who obtains market quotes from data vendors and third
parties. Any change in net unrealized gain or loss during the current period is reported in the statement of operations. Realized gains and losses on transactions are recognized in the period in which the contracts is closed. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The weighted average number of Limited and General Interests outstanding was computed for purposes of disclosing net income (loss) per weighted average
Limited and General Interest. The weighted average Limited and General Interests are equal to the number of Interests outstanding at period end, adjusted proportionately for Interests subscribed or redeemed based on their respective time outstanding
during such period. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Series A has elected not to provide a Statements of Cash Flows as permitted by Statement of Financial Accounting
Standards No.&nbsp;102, &#147;Statement of Cash Flows &#150; Exemption of Certain Enterprises and Classification of Cash Flows from Certain Securities Acquired for Resale.&#148; </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Consistent with standard business practices in the normal course of business, Series A has provided general indemnifications to the Managing Owner, its
Trading Advisor and others when they act, in good faith, in the best interests of Series A. Series A is unable to develop an estimate of the maximum potential amount of future payments that could potentially result from any hypothetical future
claim, but expects the risk of having to make any payments under these general business indemnifications to be remote. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Cash represents
amounts deposited with clearing brokers, a portion of which are restricted for purposes of meeting margin requirements, which typically range from 0% to 35% of the notional amounts of the derivatives traded, and receives interest on all cash
balances held by the clearing brokers at prevailing rates. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">

<TD WIDTH="8%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="5%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">B.</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Income Taxes </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Series A is treated as a partnership for
Federal income tax purposes. As such, Series A is not required to provide for, or pay, any Federal or state income taxes. Income tax attributes that arise from its operations are passed directly to the individual Interest holders including the
Managing Owner. Series A may be subject to other state and local taxes in jurisdictions in which it operates. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">

<TD WIDTH="5%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">C.</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Investment in WMT Campbell Pool L.L.C. </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The investment in
WMT Campbell Pool L.L.C. is reported in Series A&#146;s statement of financial condition at the net asset value as reported by the Company. Series A records its proportionate share of the Company&#146;s income or loss in the statement of operations.
Valuation of futures contracts by the Company is discussed in the notes to the Company&#146;s financial statements included in Section II of this report. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>

<TD WIDTH="5%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">D.</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Profit and Loss Allocations and Distributions </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Series A
allocates profits and losses for both financial and tax reporting purposes to its Interest holders weekly on a pro rata basis based on each owner&#146;s Interests outstanding during the week. Distributions (other than redemptions of Interests) may
be made at the sole discretion of the Managing Owner on a pro rata basis in accordance with the respective capital balances of the Interest holders. The Managing Owner does not presently intend to make any distributions. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="8%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="5%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">E.</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Foreign Currency Transaction </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Series A&#146;s functional
currency is the U.S. dollar; however, it transacts business in currencies other than the U.S. dollar. Assets and liabilities denominated in currencies other than the U.S. dollar are translated into U.S. dollars at the rates in effect at the date of
the statement of financial condition. Income and expense items denominated in currencies other than U.S. dollars are translated into U.S. dollars at the rates in effect during the period. Gains and losses resulting from the translation to U.S.
dollars are reported in income currently. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:18px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><U>FEES</U> </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>

<TD WIDTH="5%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">A.</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Organizational, Offering, General and Administrative Costs </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="2">PEG or its affiliates paid all the costs of organizing Series A and offering its Interests and continued to pay all the administrative costs incurred by the Managing Owner or its affiliates for services they performed for Series A through
September&nbsp;30, 2004. For the period October&nbsp;1, 2004 to December&nbsp;31, 2005, Preferred paid all administrative costs for services it performed for Series A. Administrative costs include, but are not limited to, those discussed in Note 4
below. Routine legal, audit, postage and other routine third party administrative costs also were paid by PEG or its affiliates through September&nbsp;30, 2004 and by Preferred for the period October&nbsp;1, 2004 to December&nbsp;31, 2005. Under the
WMT Campbell Pool L.L.C. Organization Agreement, Preferred may allocate administrative costs of the Company to Series A. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="8%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="5%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">B.</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Management and Incentive Fees </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Through March 2000, Series
A paid its Trading Advisor a management fee at an annual rate of 2% of Series A&#146;s net asset value allocated to its management. In March 2000, the management fee was reduced to 1% and in November 2001 was increased back to 2%, as defined in the
New Advisory Agreement and previously discussed in Note 1. The management fee was determined weekly and the sum of such weekly amounts was paid monthly. Series A also paid its Trading Advisor a quarterly incentive fee equal to 23% of such Trading
Advisor&#146;s &#147;New High Net Trading Profits&#148; (as defined in the New Advisory Agreement). The incentive fee accrued weekly. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">As
previously discussed in Note 1, Eagle Trading Systems was removed as the Trading Advisor effective August&nbsp;30, 2004. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Effective with
Series A&#146;s investment in the Company on December&nbsp;6, 2004, Series A is allocated its proportionate share of the Company&#146;s management fees on a pro rata basis based on Series A&#146;s pro rata capital in the Company. Incentive fees are
based on each members trading profit and loss. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">-13- </FONT></P>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><U>FEES (CONTINUED)</U> </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>

<TD WIDTH="8%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="5%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">C.</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Commissions </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Prior to January&nbsp;1, 2004, Prudential
Securities Futures Management, Inc., as Managing Owner, and the Trust entered into a brokerage agreement with PEG to act as commodity broker for each Series whereby Series A pays a fixed fee for brokerage services rendered at an annual rate of 7.75%
of Series A&#146;s net asset value. The fee is determined weekly and the sum of such weekly amounts is paid monthly. From this fee, PEG paid execution costs (including floor brokerage expenses, give-up charges and NFA, clearing and exchange fees),
as well as compensation to employees who sold Interests. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">On January&nbsp;1, 2004, PEG, a wholly owned subsidiary of PSG, transferred its
Global Derivatives Division to PFD and Pru Global Securities, LLC, two other indirect wholly-owned subsidiaries of PSG. In connection with this transfer, PEG assigned its brokerage agreement with Series A to PFD, a properly qualified futures
commission merchant. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">On October&nbsp;1, 2004, an agreement was executed between Preferred and PFD which amended and restated the brokerage
commissions which were previously paid to PFD, excluding transaction fees which will be paid to PFD. The agreement incorporates the previous PFD brokerage agreement&#146;s terms, including the total fees paid by Series A. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Effective with Series A&#146;s investment in WMT Campbell Pool L.L.C. on December&nbsp;6, 2004, Series A is allocated its proportionate share of the
Company&#146;s PFD transaction based fees on a pro rata basis based on Series A&#146;s pro rata capital in the Company. Series A continues to pay a fixed fee equal to 7.75% of its net asset value directly to the Managing Owner, less PFD transaction
based fees allocated to Series A from the Company. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:18px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><U>RELATED PARTIES</U> </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:8%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Managing Owner or third
parties engaged by the Managing Owner perform services for Series A, which include, but are not limited to: brokerage services; accounting and financial management; registrar, transfer and assignment functions: investor communications, printing and
other administrative services. As further described in Note 3, except for costs related to brokerage services, PEG, or its affiliates, or Preferred pay all the costs of these services in addition to Series A&#146;s routine operational,
administrative, legal and auditing costs. Additionally, PEG or its affiliates paid the costs associated with offering Series A&#146;s Interests. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:8%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="2">The costs charged to Series A for brokerage services for the years ended December&nbsp;31, 2005, 2004 and 2003 were $196,943, $259,266 and $421,547, respectively. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:8%"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">All of the proceeds of the offering of Series A were received in the name of Series A and were deposited in trading or cash accounts at PEG. Prior to January&nbsp;1, 2004, Series A&#146;s assets were maintained with
PEG for margin purposes and PEG credited Series A monthly with 100% of the interest it earned on the average net assets in Series A&#146;s accounts. Effective January&nbsp;1, 2004, Series A&#146;s assets are maintained with PFD and PFD credits
Series A monthly with 100% of the interest it earns on the average net assets in Series A&#146;s accounts. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>

back-to-back trading with an affiliate, Prudential-Bache Global Markets Inc. (&#147;PBGM&#148;). PBGM attempts to earn a profit on such transactions. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:8%"><FONT

between the tax basis and book basis of Interest holders&#146; capital since inception of the Trust. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:18px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="8%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Note&nbsp;7.</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><U>DERIVATIVE INSTRUMENTS AND ASSOCIATED RISKS</U> </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:8%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Series
A is exposed to various types of risks associated with the derivative instruments and related markets in which it invests as well as through its investment in WMT Campbell Pool L.L.C. These risks include, but are not limited to, risk of loss from
fluctuations in the value of derivative instruments held (market risk) and the inability of counterparties to perform under the terms of Series A&#146;s investment activities (credit risk). </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">-15- </FONT></P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" COLOR="#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>WORLD MONITOR TRUST &#150; SERIES A </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"
ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>NOTES TO FINANCIAL STATEMENTS (CONTINUED) </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P><HR WIDTH="17%" SIZE="1" NOSHADE COLOR="#000000"> <P
STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="8%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Note&nbsp;7.</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><U>DERIVATIVE INSTRUMENTS AND ASSOCIATED RISKS (CONTINUED)</U> </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="8%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="5%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">A.</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Market Risk </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Trading in futures and forward contracts
(including foreign exchange) involves entering into contractual commitments to purchase or sell a particular commodity at a specified date and price. The gross or face amount of the contracts, which is typically many times that of Series A&#146;s
net assets being traded, significantly exceeds Series A&#146;s future cash requirements since Series A intends to close out its open positions prior to settlement. As a result, Series A is generally subject only to the risk of loss arising from the
change in the value of the contracts. As such, Series A considers the &#147;fair value&#148; of its derivative instruments to be the net unrealized gain or loss on the contracts. The market risk associated with Series A&#146;s commitments to
purchase commodities is limited to the gross or face amount of the contract held. However, when Series A enters into a contractual commitment to sell commodities, it must make delivery of the underlying commodity at the contract price and then
repurchase the contract at prevailing market prices or settle in cash. Since the repurchase price to which a commodity can rise is unlimited, entering into commitments to sell commodities exposes Series A to unlimited risk. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Market risk is influenced by a wide variety of factors, including government programs and policies, political and economic events, the level and
volatility of interest rates, foreign currency exchange rates, the diversification effect among the derivative instruments Series A holds and the liquidity and inherent volatility of the markets in which Series A trades. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="8%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="5%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">B.</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Credit Risk </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">When entering into futures or forward
contracts, Series A is exposed to credit risk that the counterparty to the contract will not meet its obligations. The counterparty for futures contracts traded on United States and most foreign futures exchanges is the clearinghouse associated with
the particular exchange. In general, clearinghouses are backed by their corporate members who are required to share any financial burden resulting from the non-performance by one of their members and, as such, should significantly reduce this credit
risk. In cases where the clearinghouse is not backed by the clearing members (i.e., some foreign exchanges), it is normally backed by a consortium of banks or other financial institutions. On the other hand, there is a concentration risk on forward
transactions entered into by Series A as Series A&#146;s commodity broker (through its investment in WMT Campbell Pool LLC) (as defined in Note 4), is the sole counterparty. Series A has entered into a master netting agreement with its broker
(through its investment in WMT Campbell Pool LLC) and, as a result, when applicable, presents unrealized gains and losses on open forward positions as a net amount in the statements of financial condition. The amount at risk associated with
counterparty non-performance of all of Series A&#146;s contracts is the net unrealized gain included in the statements of financial condition; however, counterparty non-performance on only certain of Series A&#146;s contracts may result in greater
loss than non-performance on all of Series A&#146;s contracts. There can be no assurance that any counterparty, clearing member or clearinghouse will meet its obligations to Series A. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT
SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">-16- </FONT></P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" COLOR="#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>WORLD MONITOR TRUST &#150; SERIES A </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"
ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>NOTES TO FINANCIAL STATEMENTS (CONTINUED) </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P><HR WIDTH="17%" SIZE="1" NOSHADE COLOR="#000000"> <P
STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="8%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Note&nbsp;7.</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><U>DERIVATIVE INSTRUMENTS AND ASSOCIATED RISKS (CONTINUED)</U> </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="8%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="5%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">B.</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Credit Risk (Continued) </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Managing Owner attempts to
minimize both credit and market risks by requiring Series A and the Trading Advisor of WMT Campbell Pool L.L.C. to abide by various trading limitations and policies. The Managing Owner monitors compliance with these trading limitations and policies,
which include, but are not limited to, executing and clearing all trades with creditworthy counterparties; limiting the amount of margin or premium required for any one commodity or all commodity or all commodities combined; and generally limiting
transactions to contracts which are traded in sufficient volume to permit the taking and liquidating of positions. Additionally, pursuant to the advisory agreement among WMT Campbell Pool L.L.C., Preferred and the Trading Advisor, Preferred shall
automatically terminate WMT Campbell Pool L.L.C.&#146;s trading agreement if the net asset value allocated to the trading advisor declines by 40% from the value at the beginning of any year or since the effective date of the advisory agreement
(i.e., December 2004). Furthermore, the Third Amended and Restated Declaration of Trust and Trust Agreement provides that Series A will liquidate its positions, and eventually dissolve, if Series A experiences a decline in net asset value of 50%
from the value at the beginning of any year or since the commencement of trading activities. In each case, the decline in net asset value is after giving effect for distributions, contributions and redemptions. The Managing Owner may impose
additional restrictions (through modifications of trading limitations and policies) upon the trading activities of the Trading Advisor as it, in good faith, deems to be in the best interest of Series A. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:13%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Series A&#146;s futures commission merchant, in accepting orders for the purchase or sale of domestic futures contracts, is required by Commodity Futures
Trading Commission (&#147;CFTC&#148;) regulations to separately account for and segregate as belonging to Series A all assets of Series A relating to domestic futures trading and is not allowed to commingle such assets with its other assets. At
December&nbsp;31, 2005 and 2004, such segregated assets totaled $0 and $98, respectively. Part 30.7 of the CFTC regulations also requires Series A&#146;s futures commission merchant to secure assets of Series A related to foreign futures trading
which totaled $0 and $15,968 at December&nbsp;31, 2005 and 2004, respectively. There are no segregation requirements for assets related to forward trading. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">-17- </FONT></P>

schedule of investments, of WMT Campbell Pool L.L.C. (the &#147;Company&#148;) as of December&nbsp;31, 2005, and the related statements of operations and changes in Unitholders&#146; capital for the year then ended. These financial statements are
the responsibility of the Company&#146;s management. Our responsibility is to express an opinion on these financial statements based on our audit. The financial statements for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2004, including the condensed schedule
of investments for 2004, were audited by another auditor whose report dated March&nbsp;25, 2005, expressed unqualified opinions on those statements. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">We
conducted our audit in accordance with generally accepted auditing standards as established by the Auditing Standards Board (United States), and in accordance with the auditing standards of the Public Company Accounting Oversight Board (United
States). Those standards require that we plan and perform the audit to obtain reasonable assurance about whether the financial statements are free of material misstatement. The Company is not required to have, nor were we engaged to perform, an
audit of its internal control over financial reporting. Our audit included consideration of internal control over financial reporting as a basis for designing audit procedures that are appropriate in the circumstances, but not for the purpose of
expressing an opinion on the effectiveness of the Company&#146;s internal control over financial reporting. Accordingly, we express no such opinion. An audit also includes examining, on a test basis, evidence supporting the amounts and disclosures
in the financial statements, assessing the accounting principles used and significant estimates made by management, as well as evaluating the overall financial statement presentation. We believe that our audit provides a reasonable basis for our
opinion. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">In our opinion, the 2005 financial statements referred to above present fairly, in all material respects, the financial position of the Company
at December&nbsp;31, 2005, and the results of its operations and changes in Unitholders&#146; capital for the year then ended in conformity with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States of America. </FONT></P> <P

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>WMT CAMPBELL POOL L.L.C. </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"
ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>NOTES TO FINANCIAL STATEMENTS </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P><HR WIDTH="17%" SIZE="1" NOSHADE COLOR="#000000"> <P
